{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01Kt4ASjBZqgjxcDMXfUNACJ","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Now I have a good understanding of the resharding mechanism. Let me look at the issue. When resharding happens:\n\n1. `reshardLoop()` receives numShards from `reshardChan`\n2. It calls `t.shards.stop()` which:\n   - Closes `softShutdown` channel\n   - Calls `queue.FlushAndShutdown()` on each queue\n   - Waits for queues to flush with timeout (flushDeadline)\n   - If timeout, does hard shutdown\n3. Then it calls `t.shards.start(numShards)` which creates new queues\n\nThe problem might be related to how the shard assignment works. When resharding from 4 shards to 6 shards, the hash function used to determine which shard a sample goes to is:\n```\nshard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))\n```\n\nThis is done in the `enqueue` method at line 1315.\n\nNow, here's the potential issue:\n- During resharding, the old shards are being stopped and flushed\n- New shards are being created with a different number\n- The samples that were assigned to the old shards by using `ref % 4` are now being sent to new shards using `ref % 6`\n- This means the same series ref will map to different shards!\n\nHowever, when the resharding process happens, there's a potential race:\n1. `reshardLoop()` is processing the reshard request\n2. The WAL watcher or other components are still calling `enqueue()` on the old shards\n3. During the transition, samples might be enqueued to the old shards\n4. But the old shards are being shut down/flushed\n\nLet me look at the issue more closely. The key problem is that `enqueue()` checks if `softShutdown` has been closed, and if so, returns false. But if the WAL watcher or other code doesn't handle the false return properly, samples could be lost.\n\n\nThe issue described mentions \"some shards stall\" - meaning samples are stuck in pending state rather than being lost entirely. This suggests the problem isn't about samples disappearing, but rather getting blocked somewhere. During the transition between old and new shards, there's a critical window where new samples might arrive while `reshardLoop()` is calling `t.shards.stop()`. If the timing is off, samples could be enqueued to old shards that are already shutting down, or there could be a gap where new shards aren't yet ready to accept samples.\n\nLooking at the synchronization, `stop()` acquires both an RLock and then a write Lock, while `start()` takes a Lock. The CHANGELOG entry about disabling resharding during active retry backoffs suggests the real issue is that resharding shouldn't happen when the system is already under stress with retries in flight.\n\nWhen `reshardLoop()` initiates resharding by calling `t.shards.stop()`, it closes the `softShutdown` channel, which signals existing shards to reject new data. The problem emerges in the timing between when old shards stop accepting samples and new shards become ready—samples could be lost if they're rejected before the new shard queue is operational. The `stop()` function acquires a write lock and flushes all queues, then waits for completion or times out before calling `hardShutdown()`. Meanwhile, `start()` also takes the write lock to create and assign new queues. The critical issue is what happens when a sample is being enqueued during `stop()`'s wait period—the enqueue operation holds a read lock, checks if `softShutdown` is closed, and returns false, but I'm uncertain whether the sample gets properly requeued or dropped. I need to trace where `enqueue` is actually invoked from the `AppendSample` or `WriteTo` methods to understand the full flow.","signature":"EuwmCkYICxgCKkDe8Ou2HwjQSX6MxC+ly6Z7IaZLi0FUWDRgVzSsEzR26UDm1bpN8u4oJzOPSf3kJmLm0hUEiumnYzbbnlq7tO8lEgyNK94XjoeBzxffkOEaDM9nnfdjXPpwUJ8ZASIwPwQxmQbtrdhsc3DkRDGe5GN55GkyKOuSsrxrkndcL5++wYQRFxNFst8pkmNudKEWKtMljf5HqHi+CbHRKjFIWZYFHoM2r8/auahwHEczQOqApAk5sC8iPgx3hkBRsIFyTj1KABIDJ0E1J0n+K7bNRpPowGbezMTzcVkNBC5dD74YkpuWFg9MYFss1s3GdeIYo/g49g/LxaLljJuyRF8I03Da6hx94lnpXym+u1U1Tlhdj1WpTFJGMQzyJy1LOAapuNyGskP9pZYVg+kfBNNoO1y7T4FAUZKuom65SKUlnt+QvmDMO4oud63y6fC2DZS6aF+G+K5pLd4xjPlsX9tPnCpB4wTQmT1Jf/BgsbBfIJKxJAt0fZAKmLUKICYMeRIP42duqXsTXxs9KyxsD8ym1vFyoyNLnZwCU+2CSjoIhKO7JwMJaUD9E8IazhRUJsoub1gUeYiYOfBvBFlfc94JUTJfreGoUDUPoEcsqmlSWQlLOhL+iUbe6V98mARx3IZrJV2IgdNzz97pdpiKlDf+tq2fzMlf6TUcERHs/+guK0QfAjFONp4zsygOr0TTtDsyT7L9ChjsKlM7pDBiBiZsqSFN9+7nfK0EznJZAIQx4Up1MGKrz3Oi5Wi+ZTQszq/ah1mHdVFnCRDzEyhBrcCjFKECox1gwg1eJI/p4gjU4y0k0fpXRPh617PuNOcu+nWz1tWf2XA+zscNlNiqzZDeyeel3yYmSLTRBza+SM4wlyR6uTkTzE7SoyvxN7LfyLEIytruE3kxaXL8D4ai95KIXYrJ1lrAa6mnMvkabiwzeFGXWwM2oNSTVj6dCwey0dDyK9R5U7PzaBJEmQnmPwRft+GLa55c+Drj0HDkTTzLukPd50hruZvXOx+TILQOKlVfy9D9/2A5ugWETe/dp+uhnlo+LpwOGGgxd1NQg+oLsDcaetb4HX3PMsMkvHj0tXvGxmNhortU8/pkqUal1RckcDnuefhLtJXn1wND2njYqsz1j6Lmz2oD1b+X9o52bhkdjAlNOqcHzrZIO2EfbSGt8UtUMvGpPM3cDpyUcJSYxFHUtb6cDUNYkZBdX71nCd2se+oU7WsAE55VRfWMp3N8rS2faLtvqZhuzbPppZjL7FwbpbrdCHHtKO5v5y3u+tj493SF5+jNkrmuxVCWzGE50nxoCqg3igud1W74W1IuhlZqYsvC6/2Og3eIbxCpSKKrr7Q4h5zBViuqUVi3VdA4HGVtIw0E4MFdZAi2gxk7y9sFfbTxaY7AZ07xzTmgFG4Qn5uKKPtxol8eRxKfyrCZpLGx6UPqMdqkI7PMYfq+r3fR6ndF5EG+XZVglGP0iX9OFlZL9VzV6dmFbICQXW78t9F+tMZw5yGubI72/6vMGfjNrwdgsvDtUI4z9hrIKbNVTRETqQ8KcRlxZaPfO6mX+5Y0eU6J54cd9IiMuub75nvo/Dy56lN+zavz5vQyUliesr9byOU9p8K33VGKJXo5BQ9srS1wnZhRNIZRL3G668tboT6cg278XYMfUCXO7K3wuPO1+49GVNJvrnwg8foS/bFwhbbv1pkivyS7k5uxpE0tWm9rDEpZvCQXswLyLlpnpkJaQLZSZe6PMOkAguq9Bsp7JJM0Z5g1fwKR/n9K/Nq+Vsm12SUOcTOuUQo30lezx+9PzfaRZ+1Wrkd8pTCMKM8gv84DB9XQNAdfit483ojP0G5M8mN1cFVGSaK5bQZQtQLE9zbPyMyHqFvXmqC9zBQja12lBob+pJ0EDvv+ixiV4NBTrlFJEQ+An+5Kpf5+tRoe+OFohjAc9A5SpLEdH8ZOZ0Ghw+m7ZwtsoVm0BOW68fJl It will get retried.\n\t\t\tq.batch = q.batch[:len(q.batch)-1]\n```\n\nThe queue appends the sample to its batch, and if the batch is full, it tries to send it on the batchQueue channel. If the channel is blocked (default case), it removes the sample and returns false. This triggers a retry in the Append method with backoff, which will eventually succeed once the batch is processed.\n\nWhen resharding occurs, the batchQueue gets closed, so any full batches can't be sent. But partial batches still accumulate in q.batch. The FlushAndShutdown method needs to handle these remaining samples by draining them before the queue fully shuts down.\n\nLooking at the tryEnqueueingBatch logic, it attempts to send batches to batchQueue, but if the channel is full or closed, those samples get lost. The critical gap is that while FlushAndShutdown is trying to drain the partial batch, new Append calls could still be adding samples to q.batch concurrently, creating a race condition where data gets dropped. _, queue := range s.queues {\n\tgo queue.FlushAndShutdown(s.done)\n}\n\nMultiple goroutines are spawned to flush each queue concurrently. The concern is whether samples can still arrive via `Append()` while `FlushAndShutdown` executes. Looking at the shutdown sequence: `stop()` first closes `softShutdown`, which causes all `enqueue()` calls to return false, preventing new samples from being added. Then it calls `FlushAndShutdown()` on each queue. So the real question is what happens to samples already sitting in the partial batch before the shutdown signal was sent.\n\nI notice something in the `start()` method around line 1241 - `pendingSamples` is reset to 0 when shards restart. But if the old shards' partial batches haven't flushed yet, those samples are still in flight. This creates a timing issue where the metrics show pending=0 while samples from the old shards are still being processed.\n\nLooking deeper at the actual stall mechanism, the real problem appears to be in how the shard assignment works during resharding. When `enqueue()` calculates which shard a sample belongs to using `uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))`, it's using the current shard count. If resharding occurs mid-operation, a sample might be assigned to one shard based on the old shard count, but then the shard count changes before the sample actually gets enqueued. This creates a mismatch where samples could be routed to the wrong queue or get stuck in a queue that's no longer being actively processed.\n\nThe core issue is that `updateShardsLoop()` updates `t.numShards` immediately after sending the reshard request to the channel, before the actual resharding operation completes. This means there's a window where the shard calculation in `enqueue()` uses a different modulo value than what the queues array actually contains, causing samples to potentially be lost or stuck. The resharding process itself involves stopping old shards and starting new ones, but if samples are being enqueued during this transition with an incorrect shard index, they could end up in a queue that's being torn down or never properly processed. the new shards with 6 queues. When Append() retries, it calls enqueue() again, which now uses `ref % len(s.queues)` to determine the shard—this calculation happens inside enqueue() itself, not based on t.numShards. So the shard selection is dynamic based on the current queue count at the time of the call.\n\nI should look for recent changes or issue reports about resharding edge cases, particularly anything mentioning blocked operations during resharding in the The lost samples appear as stalled shards with pending samples stuck above zero but no delivery progress.\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**Location:** `storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1447-1455` in `queue.FlushAndShutdown()`\n\nThe resharding process stalls due to a **race condition in partial batch cleanup** during queue shutdown:\n\n```go\nfunc (q *queue) FlushAndShutdown(done <-chan struct{}) {\n    for q.tryEnqueueingBatch(done) {\n        time.Sleep(time.Second)\n    }\n    q.batchMtx.Lock()\n    defer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n    q.batch = nil                    // <-- BUG: Discards unsent samples\n    close(q.batchQueue)\n}\n```\n\n### Failure Scenario\n\n1. **Resharding triggered** (e.g., 4→6 shards): `updateShardsLoop()` detects need to reshard\n   - Sends desired shard count to `reshardChan`\n   - `reshardLoop()` begins shutdown of old shards\n\n2. **Old queue shutdown begins**: `shards.stop()` is called\n   - Closes `softShutdown` channel (prevents new enqueues)\n   - Spawns goroutines calling `queue.FlushAndShutdown()` for each queue\n   - Waits for completion with `flushDeadline` timeout (default: 1 minute)\n\n3. **Partial batch accumulation**: Old queue has partial batch with unsent samples\n   - `tryEnqueueingBatch()` attempts to send batch to `batchQueue` channel\n   - Channel is full (all downstream `runShard()` workers are busy)\n   - Returns true to retry (line 1475)\n   - Loop sleeps 1 second\n\n4. **Hard shutdown timeout expires**: Before partial batch flushes\n   - `stop()` timeout is reached (flushDeadline)\n   - Calls `hardShutdown()` which cancels the context passed to `runShard()`\n   - Signals the `done` channel\n\n5. **Critical bug triggered**:\n   - `tryEnqueueingBatch()` receives `<-done` signal (line 1469)\n   - Returns false (line 1472) - exits flush retry loop\n   - `q.batch = nil` executes (line 1453)\n   - **All samples in the partial batch are permanently lost**\n   - Never reaches `runShard()`, never tracked in failure metrics\n   - Queue is closed (line 1454)\n\n6. **New shards start** with `pendingSamples` reset to 0\n   - Metrics show 0 pending, masking the data loss\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Code References\n\n1. **Queue Shutdown Logic** (`storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1269-1305`)\n   - `shards.stop()`: Initiates soft shutdown, spawns FlushAndShutdown goroutines, waits with timeout\n   - Relevant: Hard shutdown triggered if flush exceeds `flushDeadline`\n\n2. **Partial Batch Loss** (`storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1447-1477`)\n   - `queue.FlushAndShutdown()`: Attempts to flush partial batch with retries\n   - `tryEnqueueingBatch()`: Returns false when hard shutdown signal received, exiting retry loop\n   - Missing: Logic to track/log samples lost in partial batch\n\n3. **Shard Worker** (`storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1491-1600`)\n   - `runShard()`: Receives batches from `batchQueue` channel\n   - When context cancelled, drops remaining samples and logs error\n   - But samples in *partial batch* (not yet in channel) are not counted\n\n4. **Metrics Reset** (`storage/remote/queue_manager.go:1237-1266`)\n   - `shards.start()`: Creates new queues and sets `pendingSamples.Set(0)` (line 1241)\n   - Timing issue: Old shards' remaining samples may still be pending when metric is reset\n\n### Timing Sensitivity\n\nThe bug manifests intermittently due to race conditions:\n\n**Conditions Required:**\n- Resharding occurs while old queue has partial batch (non-empty `q.batch`)\n- `batchQueue` channel fills up faster than `runShard()` workers can drain it\n- Hard shutdown timeout (default 1 minute) expires before batch can be flushed\n- Network latency/remote endpoint slowness backs up the pipeline\n\n**Why It's Intermittent:**\n- Depends on when resharding happens relative to network conditions\n- Depends on how full the queue is at reshard time\n- Depends on remote storage response times\n- More likely when targets frequently added/removed (triggering resharding)\n- More likely with slow remote endpoints or high latency networks\n\n## Affected Components\n\n### Primary Files\n- `storage/remote/queue_manager.go` - Queue management, resharding logic\n  - `QueueManager` struct (line 417)\n  - `shards` struct (line 1209)\n  - `queue` struct (line 1343)\n  - Resharding functions (lines 1057-1199)\n  - Queue flush logic (lines 1445-1477)\n\n### Related Components\n- `tsdb/wlog/watcher.go` - WAL Watcher that calls `Append()` and retries\n  - Should detect retries but lost samples bypass this\n- Remote write metrics:\n  - `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` - Reset to 0 when new shards start\n  - `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_dropped_total` - Not incremented for lost partials\n  - `prometheus_remote_storage_sent_batch_duration_seconds` - Shows no activity when samples stall\n\n## Why Metrics Show Stall\n\n1. **Stalled shards appear to have pending samples** (>0)\n   - WAL Watcher hasn't retried the lost samples yet (they were dequeued)\n   - Or WAL replay is catching up slowly\n\n2. **No progress on delivery**\n   - The partial batch samples never reached remote storage\n   - Never appear in failed metrics or logs\n   - Metrics reset when new shards start (line 1241)\n\n3. **Intermittent nature explains variability**\n   - Only affects samples in partial batches during unlucky reshard timing\n   - May only lose tens or hundreds of samples, not entire queue\n   - Lost samples not tracked = mysterious stalls\n\n## Recommended Diagnostics\n\nTo confirm this root cause:\n\n### 1. Check Logs for Reshard/Shutdown Patterns\n```\nLook for sequence:\n  \"Resharding queues\" from=4 to=6\n  \"Failed to flush all X on shutdown\" (if hard shutdown was triggered)\n\nTimeline gap between reshard message and next samples indicates loss window\n```\n\n### 2. Monitor Timing Metrics\n```\nTrack:\n  - Time between \"Resharding\" log and \"Resharding done\" completion\n  - If takes >50 seconds, approaching hard shutdown timeout\n  - Number of shards with samples_pending after reshard\n```\n\n### 3. Enable Debug Logs for Queue Manager\n```\nLook for:\n  \"Currently resharding, skipping.\" - indicates resharding already in progress\n  \"QueueManager.calculateDesiredShards\" - shows shard calc details\n  \"tryEnqueueingBatch\" attempts (would need code instrumentation)\n```\n\n### 4. Create Test Case for Intermittent Reproduction\n```\nTrigger by:\n  - Rapidly add/remove targets (force resharding)\n  - Slow remote write endpoint\n  - High sample rate\n  - Restart during heavy reshard activity\n```\n\n## Fix Strategy\n\n### Short-term Diagnostic Fix\nAdd logging in `FlushAndShutdown()` to detect partial batch loss:\n\n```go\nfunc (q *queue) FlushAndShutdown(done <-chan struct{}) {\n    for q.tryEnqueueingBatch(done) {\n        time.Sleep(time.Second)\n    }\n    q.batchMtx.Lock()\n    defer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n\n    if len(q.batch) > 0 {\n        // Log the samples that are being lost\n        q.qm.logger.Error(\"Samples lost during hard shutdown\",\n            \"count\", len(q.batch))\n    }\n    q.batch = nil\n    close(q.batchQueue)\n}\n```\n\n### Recommended Long-term Fixes\n\n1. **Force final flush attempt after hard shutdown**\n   - Add one more `tryEnqueueingBatch` call after receiving `<-done` signal\n   - Accept samples will be dropped but ensure they're counted in metrics\n   - Increment `failedSamplesTotal` for proper accounting\n\n2. **Separate metric tracking**\n   - Add new metric: `remote_storage_samples_lost_on_hard_shutdown`\n   - Decouple from `failedSamplesTotal` (those are network failures)\n   - Alert ops when samples lost during resharding\n\n3. **Increase soft shutdown timeout or use two-phase approach**\n   - Current 1-minute flush deadline may be too aggressive\n   - Or implement soft-timeout followed by a final grace period\n   - Give partial batches fair chance to flush\n\n4. **Prevent concurrent reshard/stop**\n   - Add mutex to prevent reshardLoop and Stop() from running simultaneously\n   - Related to CHANGELOG issue #5460: \"Prevent reshard concurrent with calling stop\"\n\n## Summary Table\n\n| Aspect | Finding |\n|--------|---------|\n| **Root Cause** | Samples in partial batches discarded when hard shutdown timeout expires |\n| **Location** | `queue.FlushAndShutdown()` at line 1453 |\n| **Impact** | Data loss during resharding; appears as metrics stall |\n| **Frequency** | Intermittent; depends on timing and network conditions |\n| **Detection** | No error logs; metrics reset masks loss; WAL may show unexpected gap |\n| **Fix Complexity** | Medium - requires metric tracking + flush logic changes |\n| **Severity** | High - silent data loss during cluster operations |\n\n## References\n\n- CHANGELOG entries mentioning related issues:\n  - \"Remote-write: Fix deadlock when stopping a shard. #10279\"\n  - \"Remote Write: Disable resharding during active retry backoffs #13562\"\n  - \"Remote_write: Prevent reshard concurrent with calling stop #5460\"\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":6924,"cache_read_input_tokens":77571,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":6924},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"06cb86ea-cece-4d3d-ae40-cea5f68d21e4","uuid":"7cadd1d6-e385-43cb-bd8b-bb9d71106632"}

{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_014V5qyhqZuMytzVJqCwV9R9","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Perfect! I've completed a thorough investigation of the Prometheus remote-write queue resharding issue. Let me summarize what I found:\n\n## Key Findings:\n\n1. **Root Cause**: The stall happens because partial batches (incomplete sample batches) in queue buffers are permanently discarded when a hard shutdown timeout expires during resharding, without being tracked in any metrics or logged.\n\n2. **Mechanism**: When resharding occurs:\n   - Old shards try to flush their queues\n   - If the batchQueue fills up and can't accept more batches, the retry loop sleeps\n   - If the hard shutdown timeout (flushDeadline) expires before the partial batch flushes\n   - The code receives the done signal and exits the retry loop\n   - Then it sets `q.batch = nil`, permanently losing any samples in the partial batch\n\n3. **Why It's Intermittent**: It only happens if:\n   - Resharding occurs when partial batches exist in queues\n   - The batchQueue channel fills up\n   - Hard shutdown timeout expires before flush completes\n   - This is timing-dependent on network conditions\n\n4. **Why Metrics Show Stall**: \n   - The lost samples were never sent to remote storage\n   - They're not counted in any \"failed\" metrics (bypassed runShard)\n   - pendingSamples metric is reset to 0 when new shards start\n   - So it appears as if nothing happened, but samples are missing\n\nThe investigation report provides:\n- Detailed code references with line numbers\n- The exact sequence of events that causes the stall\n- Why the issue is intermittent\n- Diagnostic steps to confirm the root cause\n- Fix strategies (short-term and long-term)\n- Relevant CHANGELOG references to related issues\n\nThis is a complete investigation as requested by the user, with no code changes, just
